For core providers, it directly instantiates them:\\n   - \\\"SUN\\\" → sun.security.provider.Sun\\n   - \\\"SunRsaSign\\\" → sun.security.rsa.SunRsaSign\\n   - \\\"SunJCE\\\" → com.sun.crypto.provider.SunJCE\\n   - \\\"SunJSSE\\\" → sun.security.ssl.SunJSSE\\n   - \\\"SunEC\\\" → sun.security.ec.SunEC\\n   - \\\"Apple\\\" → apple.security.AppleProvider (via reflection for platform compatibility)\\n\\nFor other providers, it uses ServiceLoader and legacy reflection-based loading. The ProviderConfig also tracks loading state to prevent recursion and implements caching with volatile Provider field.\\n\\n**Provider Implementations:**\\n\\n3. **Sun Provider** (sun/security/provider/Sun.java): Implements core algorithms including DSA key generation, DSA signing, SHA-1/MD5/SHA-2/SHA-3 digests, SecureRandom, X.509 certificate handling, and keystore support (PKCS12, JKS, DKS). Services are registered via helper methods ps() and psA().\\n\\n6. **SunJSSE Provider** (sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java): Implements SSL/TLS factories including KeyManagerFactory (SunX509, NewSunX509/PKIX), TrustManagerFactory (SunX509, PKIX variants), SSLContext factories for TLSv1/1.1/1.2/1.3, DTLSv1.0/1.2, and PKCS12 KeyStore support. Works with ProviderConfig to implement semi-eager loading, where providers are loaded only when actually needed. The ProviderList handles adding/removing providers, converting configurations to loaded providers, and managing provider preference order.\\n\\n**Service Registration Flow:**\\nEach provider's constructor calls putService() for each cryptographic service it provides. The putService() method (Provider.java:1221) registers the Service in an internal serviceMap indexed by type and algorithm name, and also stores property strings for compatibility. Uses custom ProviderService and ProviderServiceA inner classes that extend Provider.Service.\\n\\n**Supporting Infrastructure:**\\n\\n8. **SunEntries** (sun/security/provider/SunEntries.java): Defines the set of Service objects for the Sun provider, including digest algorithms, signatures, key factories, keystores, certificate-related services, and secure random implementations.\\n\\n9. **ProviderList** (sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages the ordered list of providers configured via java.security file. Works with ProviderConfig to implement semi-eager loading, where providers are loaded only when actually needed. The ProviderList handles adding/removing providers, converting configurations to loaded providers, and managing provider preference order.\\n\\n**Service Registration Flow:**\\nEach provider's constructor calls putService() for each cryptographic service it provides. The putService() method (Provider.java:1221) registers the Service in an internal serviceMap indexed by type and algorithm name, and also stores property strings for compatibility. Providers can also define custom Service subclasses (like SunEC's ProviderService) to override the newInstance() method for dynamic instantiation logic.\\n\\n**Lazy Loading Flow:**\\nWhen Security.getProvider(name) is called, it triggers ProviderConfig.getProvider(), which either returns a cached Provider instance or instantiates the provider for the first time using the switch-based mapping. This lazy approach improves JVM startup time by only loading providers that are actually used.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
